1.1  Analyzing a problem

The raw materials that are used to solve a problem are known as the 'input'. 
The result obtained after solving a problem is known as the 'output'. Converting 
input to output is called the 'process'. A process takes place step by step and it is 
(cid:89)(cid:72)(cid:85)(cid:92)(cid:3)(cid:76)(cid:80)(cid:83)(cid:82)(cid:85)(cid:87)(cid:68)(cid:81)(cid:87)(cid:3)(cid:87)(cid:82)(cid:3)(cid:88)(cid:81)(cid:71)(cid:72)(cid:85)(cid:86)(cid:87)(cid:68)(cid:81)(cid:71)(cid:3)(cid:87)(cid:75)(cid:72)(cid:3)(cid:82)(cid:85)(cid:71)(cid:72)(cid:85)(cid:3)(cid:82)(cid:73)(cid:3)(cid:87)(cid:75)(cid:72)(cid:3)(cid:83)(cid:85)(cid:82)(cid:70)(cid:72)(cid:86)(cid:86)(cid:17)(cid:3)(cid:58)(cid:75)(cid:72)(cid:81)(cid:3)(cid:68)(cid:81)(cid:68)(cid:79)(cid:92)(cid:93)(cid:76)(cid:81)(cid:74)(cid:3)(cid:68)(cid:3)(cid:83)(cid:85)(cid:82)(cid:69)(cid:79)(cid:72)(cid:80)(cid:15)(cid:3)

    envelope
5. Sticking the stamp

Problem 7 :

Finding whether a number is odd or even

Input :  

Number

Process :  

Dividing the number by 2

Deciding that the number is even if
the remainder = 0

Deciding that the number is odd if the remainder = 1

Output :  

Indicating whether the number is odd or even

1.2  Problem Solving using Algorithms

An
An  algorithm  is  a  method  to  show  the  steps  in  solving  a  problem.
algorithm is a step-by-step procedure for solving a problem. The need for this is to 
present a way to solve the problem with a plan.

1.3 Representation of an algorithm

Flow charts and pseudo codes are used as tools to present an algorithm to 

make the algorithm understand better.

For free distribution

9

1.3.1

Flowcharts

Flowcharts are used to present how the algorithm is built step by step in a 
dramatic manner. The symbols given in table are used to indicate different functions. 
(cid:11)(cid:54)(cid:72)(cid:72)(cid:3)(cid:55)(cid:68)(cid:69)(cid:79)(cid:72)(cid:3)(cid:20)(cid:17)(cid:20)(cid:12)

Symbol

Table 1.1

Function
Start or end

Input or output

Process

Decision

Flow direction

Connector

Sequence

In sequence the steps from the beginning to the end are executed in order.

E.g. 1 - Finding the area of a circle.

Start

Input the radius of the circle

Calculate the area of the circle

Output the area of the circle

End

1.3.2 Pseudo codes

When an algorithm is presented in simple English terms it is called a pseudo 
code. Pseudo codes are independent of a computer language. Pseudo codes can be

Following are some of the facts about the above pseudo code.
²

Total, Average and Number are variables.

²

²

²

²

²

²

²

²

²

°  When values are assigned to number variable, the value of Total, Average 

and n variables change.

n indicates the number of repetitions. (Number of times the loop is executed)

The statements  Total  =  0  and  Average  =  0,  makes  starting  values  of  these 
variables assigned as 0.

°  Hence, the initial value of Total and Average are 0s.

The statement n = 1, makes the starting value of n is assigned to 1.
(cid:81)(cid:3)(cid:31)(cid:32)(cid:3)(cid:20)(cid:19)(cid:3)(cid:76)(cid:86)(cid:3)(cid:87)(cid:75)(cid:72)(cid:3)(cid:70)(cid:82)(cid:81)(cid:71)(cid:76)(cid:87)(cid:76)(cid:82)(cid:81)(cid:3)(cid:87)(cid:75)(cid:68)(cid:87)(cid:3)(cid:86)(cid:75)(cid:82)(cid:88)(cid:79)(cid:71)(cid:3)(cid:69)(cid:72)(cid:3)(cid:86)(cid:68)(cid:87)(cid:76)(cid:86)(cid:191)(cid:72)(cid:71)(cid:17)

WHILE n <= 10 indicates that the loop n should be repeated until value of n is 
10.

°  Repetition occurs when the value of n is 10 or less than 10. This means, 
till the condition n <=10 is true, repetition occurs. When the value of n 
becomes 11, the repetition stops. Then the condition becomes false. 

READ denotes getting a value for Number variable.

Total  =  Total  +  Number  denotes  the
present  value  of  Total  is  added  to 
number  and  the  resultant  value  is 
assigned on the new value of Total.

n  =  n  +  1  calculates  the  number  of 
repetitions. 1 is added to the present 
value  of  n  and  the  result  is  assigned 
to n.

ENDWHILE  indicates  the  limit  to 
end  repetition.  Hence,  only  READ 
number, Total = Total + Number and n = n + 1 are repeated till the condition n 
(cid:31)(cid:32)(cid:3)(cid:20)(cid:19)(cid:3)(cid:76)(cid:86)(cid:3)(cid:73)(cid:88)(cid:79)(cid:191)(cid:79)(cid:79)(cid:72)(cid:71)(cid:17)

²
When the repetition stops, the value of n is 11 and the condition is false. 
² (cid:37)(cid:92)(cid:3)(cid:36)(cid:89)(cid:72)(cid:85)(cid:68)(cid:74)(cid:72)(cid:3)(cid:32)(cid:3)(cid:55)(cid:82)(cid:87)(cid:68)(cid:79)(cid:18)(cid:11)(cid:81)(cid:3)(cid:16)(cid:3)(cid:20)(cid:12)(cid:3)(cid:15)(cid:3)(cid:191)(cid:81)(cid:68)(cid:79)(cid:3)(cid:89)(cid:68)(cid:79)(cid:88)(cid:72)(cid:3)(cid:82)(cid:73)(cid:3)(cid:55)(cid:82)(cid:87)(cid:68)(cid:79)(cid:3)(cid:76)(cid:86)(cid:3)(cid:71)(cid:76)(cid:89)(cid:76)(cid:71)(cid:72)(cid:71)(cid:3)(cid:69)(cid:92)(cid:3)(cid:11)(cid:81)(cid:3)(cid:177)(cid:3)(cid:20)(cid:12)(cid:3)(cid:68)(cid:81)(cid:71)(cid:3)(cid:87)(cid:75)(cid:68)(cid:87)(cid:3)

3. Logical operators

Logical operators are used to combine two or more expressions. For further 

study on this refer basic logic gates that you learnt in Grade 10.

iii)  NOT operator

A True expression is always evaluated as false with a NOT operator while a 

false expression is always evaluated as true.

1.8.2 Selection in repetition

E.g. - ; Var X : Array[1..5] of integer;

Only data items which belong to the same type can be stored in the array.

Any element of the array can be accessed randomly. Hence, an array can be 

accessed easily through a repetition control structure. 

E.g. - Entering Maths marks of 40 students into an array

var   maths : array[0..39] of integer;

for i :

i,marks : integer; 
}
 0 to 39 do
begin

writeln(‘Enter marks’);
read(marks);
maths[i] :

 marks;

}

end;

1.10.1 Types of sub program

There are two types of sub programs in addition to the main program. A 
sub program which returns an output back to the main program and a sub program 
which does not return an output back to the main program. A sub program which 
returns an output back is called a Function and a sub program which does not give 
an output is called a Procedure.
